I was disappointed that this one was designed so poorly in comparison.<br /><br />The main grip I have is that whoever designed the 12-setting stubble guard for this thing needs to go back to engineering school. The guard does NOT completely cover and wrap around the blade head. This causes two enormous problems. One, if you apply too much pressure while using it, the guard flexes, temporarily allowing it to get closer to your face and causing patchiness.<br /><br />The second problem, however, is just mind-boggling in its stupidity. Because the stubble guard doesn't completely wrap around the blade head and leaves it exposed, if you tilt it at the wrong angle, the full unguarded blade head can easily come into contact with your face, essentially shaving you at a 0 according to the blade settings. Unless you have the hands of world class surgeon, you're GOING to occasionally tilt the trimmer a little, causing the unguarded blade to come into contact with your face and ruining whatever length your were trying for.<br /><br />I can't speak to the beard guard, because I don't keep my beard long enough to utilize it. But if you're planning on using this thing for any kind of short beard or stubble work, don't bother. It cannot be used that way because of the poorly designed stubble guard. You WILL simply end up with a patchy face.

  887. This is a great trimmer for a great price. It's also versatile. Here are my favorite features:<br /><br />* You can use it either cordless (up to 35 minutes they say) or by plugging in. The latter option is actually a good feature. Some other cordless trimmers of this kind CANNOT be used plugged in, which is really annoying when you find your trimmer out of batteries and need it in a pinch. So kudos to Philips for thinking it through and allowing use while it's plugged in.<br /><br />* The extra blades work well. I mainly use the standard width blade, but the wider one works for shaving the head (believe it or not) and the thinner one is good for detailing. Used the nose trimmer once and it was fine (I hate nose trimmers). The blades are easy to remove and attach; the only problem is that you have to find a place to store them without creating clutter.<br /><br />* The plastic attachments (which determine blade height) work as advertised, but you need to make sure you don't accidentally compress the button that lets it slide to a different setting.<br /><br />* It's pretty quiet overall and seems to charge fast.<br /><br />* It works on the head. I know I said this briefly above, but it deserves a bit more mention. I took an older version of this same trimmer on a trip with me to England because my normal hair clippers could not operate on British power outlets. (Yes, I cut my own hair; yes, I'm damn good at it.) This Philips Norelco is compatible with the full range of voltage and thus can be used in Europe or Asia as well as North America without problems; all you need is an outlet adapter (*not* converter). In short, this thing did a great job on my hair. And if a multi-groomer can give a white-collar guy a passable haircut, it must be pretty good.

  1349. This Philips Norelco rechargeable grooming kit came my way at a good time, because I was trying to grow a short beard for the first time in my life (not just a goatee). Overall, it's a well-rounded shaving kit that does a good job. Just remember, the \\"all-in-one\\" kit doesn't contain an everyday razor that you can use for a general shave (though the included precision trimmer does a passable job of clearing off the stubble en masse).<br /><br />For me, the biggest thing about this kit was learning how to use all the pieces -- it takes a while, especially if you're like me and skim the directions. Interchanging the pieces can be a bit of a hassle when you're trying to get ready in the morning, but it's worth changing them out because each one does a solid job at what it's designed to do.<br /><br />I like keeping my beard very short, so the \\"stubble comb\\" and \\"beard trimmer\\" pieces are the ones I often use. The stubble comb slides into a groove on the back of the razor and offers lengths of one through 12, with one being the closest shave. You'll want to angle the comber on your face so that it cuts to the length you selected, something I didn't figure out right away.<br /><br />For those of you with lengthier beards, the \\"beard and mustache comb\\"/\\"beard trimmer\\" combo is the one you'll want to use. The latter piece slides into the aforementioned grooves on the shaver in the same way as the stubble comb, offering shaving lengths of one through 18. Using this piece at level one gives my beard and sideburns the stubble length I like.<br /><br />The smaller precision trimmer does an excellent job of outlining your facial hair and tidying up those outlying areas. Be careful with this piece; it's sharp and I cut myself with it a few times. You can also use the full-size trimmer for the same purpose.<br /><br />The kit also includes a \\"nose/ear hair trimmer\\" attachment that works well.<br /><br />The waterproof feature is a nice touch that helps prevent too much hair accumulation on the pieces. Be sure to rinse off the attachments before you take them off.<br /><br />This shaver holds its charge for 35 minutes after charging for 10 hours, and it isn't overly loud. Overall, when I compare this grooming kit to the clunky, battery-operated Wahl stubble trimmer I own, there really is no comparison. The most important advice I can offer regarding this kit is to use all of the included components to see what works best for you. After getting used to the various functions, you'll see that this is a well-rounded grooming kit that accommodates a multitude of facial hair styles.lation on the pieces. Then you grasp the depth adjustment plasticpiece in the other hand. Now you slide the edges of the plastic piece into the corresponding slots in the shaver.... You're welcome.
